< Text>
Nice place to boondock. You have to bring what ever you need and take it back out. RV must be self-contained. Hot spring across the road from the camp is beautiful. Hiked around the area a bit. Irrigation on one side of the canal to grow carrots and desert on the other side of the canal. Friendly neighbors. Lots of bike riders.</Text>

< text>
One of the best camping experiences of my life. Nobody bothered us, the hot springs were fantastic, and being out there in the desert felt like we were on the moon. We had the whole place to ourselves and it felt great. Keep your campfires low, because the surrounding brush can get very dry.<//text>

Well the first few nights I was there it was nice ... went to the hot tub in the evenings... then people came into the pools and we're smoking cigarettes... I said to the one local gentleman would you mind not smoking... he was blowing it in my face and told me to suck it up... then there was a guy there hacking and coughing and spitting it on the ground where everyone walked... then a little while later there was a guy blowing his nose onto the ground where you walked honestly people are so inconsiderate.... I went there to relax and I wanted to feel like I was doing something for my body by soaking in the mineral water ...well it was sort of counterproductive... it was my thought that you're not allowed to smoke in a public place and I consider that a public place... BLM really should post a no smoking sign in the pool area... and I guess that's all I got to say about that ...won't be returning but I'm sure the locals will be happy about that... they seem to want to dominate the pools with they're smoking and bringing their dogs into the pools...  they don't  volunteer to clean the pools but they sure like to use them...<//Text>

106988748623931162126< /UserId.>
<name>Greg Kendall</name><time>1515705866493<//time><rate>3<//rate>< review>
Holtville hot springs is interesting. There are soak pools here and a sprinkler type device for cooling off. There are restrooms here too. Across the road is a Long Term Visitors Area (LTVA) where you can pay $180 and stay in a self-contained RV for an entire season. Or you can pay $40 for 14 days. Many Canadian Snowbirds stay here in the winter and soak their retirement days away in the cement tubs.  It seems very pleasant. It's desert land so be prepared for that. It's not far from the freeway exit. On the south side of the freeway is free BLM land for camping.<//review>

< Review>
This was the first time my husband and I have been to picazio. I ordered the cauliflower crispy tacos with a side order of french fries and my husband had the corn. My cauliflower crispy tacos were stuffed with cauliflower and topped with a crispy coleslaw.  The corn tortillas had spicy hot sauce included and the french fries were sliced very thin hot crispy and spicy. Just delicious. I would have a hard time going there again and not ordering the cauliflower tacos. The corn my husband had was absolutely delicious. < text>
I would hope i can give a 0 star to this place. For a toyota corolla, i ended up paying about $400 for ONLY 4 days.

I am a student, I was trying to get a cheap rental car.
On the website, they claimed unlimited mileage was $6 per day. It was extremely cheap, so I fell into their trap.

this is how they con me.

lets calculated how much l lost:
base price:                                                   $6 per day
insurance(they said covers everything): $21.99* per day
add another 400 miles:                              $15 per day
Total per day:                                               $ 42.99 per day !!!
I scratched a little on the bumper:    paid another $250
Yes, that insurance DOES NOT COVER EVERYTHING!!!!
for 4 days:                                  42.99 x 3 + 250=$419.32

Not just only me argued with them, when I returned the car, there was an Indian gentleman argued with them of the unlimited mileage they lied, and another Asian lady was arguing about the price they change during a phone call with them the day before.
As a car rental company, they provide extremely bad customer service.
In conclusion, please do not rent their car, this is a very small company and they want to earn fast money.
I have the videos of 3 parties arguing with NU car rental/Deanza car rental. Feel free to email me for more information and / or videos.< /text>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
This trail is perfect for a leisurely walk with beautiful coastal cliff scenery. The trail is flat with little elevation gain unless you decide to climb down to the water (we did!). I loved the artistic bench areas to stop and soak in the sights. Dogs are allowed on leash, and our puppy loved the various brush and vegetation along the way. Most of the trail is safely away from the cliffs, but there are short smaller side trails that take you closer to the edge if you're interested in a better view. It's probably safest to keep children on the main trail and dogs securely on leash. We saw large birds swooping overhead as well as sea lions (or seals?) basking in the sun on the rocks. Squirrels ran from hole to hole. So there's lots of wildlife to observe and enjoy. The coastal breeze keeps you cool, but you might want sun screen since there's little to no shade. Overall, it's a very pleasurable, easy walk.</Review>

<rating>5<//rating><Text>No trip to the Cambria and Central Coast Area should be complete without a visit to the bluff Trail. This is a one-of-a-kind experience on the fiscalini Ranch Preserve which protects over 400 Acres of beautiful Coastal land. This easy to find & walk Trail starts on Windsor Road highlighting the coastline which gives you the most beautiful views of cliffs, Canyons boulders flora and fauna. This is where mountains, forests and the ocean meet. On a cool January evening you'll find green grass Meadows meeting the rugged cliffs along the coastline. Explorer the small little Trails off the main trail which leads you closer to the cliffs, but be careful! They can be pretty steep. One of my favorite parts of this Trail are the unique benches you'll find scattered throughout. Each one is dedicated to a different family or person but made in such Grand and special ways. They are big benches and when you sit on them you feel like you're sitting on a throne and the best part is they give you the best views of the ocean. Pack a lunch, pack some snacks and water and enjoy the beautiful views. Dog friendly, must be on a leash. Wheelchair and bicycle accessible!</Text>< Pics>

< review>
Pretty good sushi! Was full after 2 veggie rolls (the lounge lizard and the green monster specifically) and a hand roll (the lobster - not my favorite item).
The lobster is like a shredded "lobster salad", I just prefer chunks of lobster is all. The Cocomo was delicious and sweet and crunchy. The tasmanian devil was really good with layers of flavor. Not enough salmon on the menu (according to my salmon loving guest) and the specialty rolls were really expensive (paying $16-17 for a  special roll, which we usually do at sushi places, wasnt happening here). The parking is ample, and the waiters were very nice and attentive the whole time.</review>

< name>
Carlyn Stech< /name>
<Date>1559352152995</Date><rate>2< /rate>< text>
This is a review based on the food and service after they moved to their new location. There has obviously been a lot of staffing changes including the servers that I have seen at the previous location. The current staff does not know the menu and are not entirely helpful. The wait is long and they seem very disorganized. Instead of dining in I decided to order pick-up today which took twice as long as it should have on the phone. I was told it would be longer than usual preparation time and they would be ready at 5:55, which was fine. I came to pick up my to-go order at exactly that time. When they found my order I discovered the rolls were much warmer than they should be! My food was likely sitting out for quite some time. If I choose to eat raw fish I expect it to be sushi grade and kept at an appropriate temperature!

I enjoy the rolls at Sushi Lounge, despite their predictable American spin, but I will not choose to dine here any longer. If you're looking for an authentic experience, great sushi and great service, I suggest Ichizen by Five Guys and Michael's. You won't be getting any asparagus there, though!

Goodbye Poway Sushi Lounge, you've lost my business. Please train your staff and get your act together.<//text>

< text>
Most of the menu consists of "unique" rolls, but I thought the execution was pretty mediocre. Sauces were watery, leaving the roll sitting in the sauce and becoming difficult to pick up without falling apart. Flavors and textures were mushy and muddled, leaving me to wonder how long they sat out before our server brought them out. Our server forgot about parts of our order, but we just let it go since we were unimpressed with the rest of the food. Won't be coming back, there are too many other good sushi places in town.<//text>
